<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="South_Carolina">South Carolina</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=East_Coast_Greenway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: South Carolina">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:317px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Map-david-quick-photo.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="345" data-file-width="520" height="209" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Map-david-quick-photo.jpg/315px-Map-david-quick-photo.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Map-david-quick-photo.jpg/473px-Map-david-quick-photo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/4/49/Map-david-quick-photo.jpg 2x" width="315"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Map-david-quick-photo.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Showing the map of the <a href="/wiki/Charleston,_South_Carolina" title="Charleston, South Carolina">Charleston</a> segment of the East Coast Greenway at an event in Charleston</div></div></div>
<p>The 270-mile (430 km) trail travels along <a href="/wiki/South_Carolina" title="South Carolina">South Carolina</a>'s coast through <a href="/wiki/Myrtle_Beach,_South_Carolina" title="Myrtle Beach, South Carolina">Myrtle Beach</a>, <a href="/wiki/Georgetown,_South_Carolina" title="Georgetown, South Carolina">Georgetown</a>, <a href="/wiki/Charleston,_South_Carolina" title="Charleston, South Carolina">Charleston</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Beaufort,_South_Carolina" title="Beaufort, South Carolina">Beaufort</a>. The route is 15% off-road, with 20% more in development.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li>North Myrtle Beach Greenway, <a href="/wiki/Barefoot_Landing" title="Barefoot Landing">Barefoot Resort</a> Segment – <a href="/wiki/North_Myrtle_Beach,_South_Carolina" title="North Myrtle Beach, South Carolina">North Myrtle Beach</a></li>
<li>Colonel Robert Bell Pass Trail – <a href="/wiki/Myrtle_Beach,_South_Carolina" title="Myrtle Beach, South Carolina">Myrtle Beach</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Robert_Grissom_Parkway" title="Robert Grissom Parkway">Grissom Parkway Trail</a> – Myrtle Beach</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Harrelson_Boulevard" title="Harrelson Boulevard">Harrelson Boulevard Trail</a> – Myrtle Beach</li>
<li>King's Highway Trail – Myrtle Beach</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Waccamaw_Neck" title="Waccamaw Neck">Waccamaw Neck</a> Bikeway – <a href="/wiki/Litchfield_Beach,_South_Carolina" title="Litchfield Beach, South Carolina">Litchfield</a>, <a href="/wiki/Murrells_Inlet,_South_Carolina" title="Murrells Inlet, South Carolina">Murrells Inlet</a>, to <a href="/wiki/Pawleys_Island,_South_Carolina" title="Pawleys Island, South Carolina">Pawleys Island</a></li>
<li>Ben Sawyer Boulevard Sidepath – <a href="/wiki/Mount_Pleasant,_South_Carolina" title="Mount Pleasant, South Carolina">Mount Pleasant</a> to <a href="/wiki/Sullivan%27s_Island,_South_Carolina" title="Sullivan's Island, South Carolina">Sullivan's Island</a></li>
<li>Garret P. Wonders Memorial Bike/Ped Lane – <a href="/wiki/Charleston,_South_Carolina" title="Charleston, South Carolina">Charleston</a> to Mount Pleasant</li>
<li>East Bay Trail – Charleston</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/West_Ashley_Greenway" title="West Ashley Greenway">West Ashley Greenway</a> – Charleston</li>
<li>New River Trail – <a href="/wiki/Bluffton,_South_Carolina" title="Bluffton, South Carolina">Bluffton</a></li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Southeast_region">Southeast region</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=East_Coast_Greenway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Southeast region">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Georgia">Georgia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=East_Coast_Greenway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Georgia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:News-570x479.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="479" data-file-width="570" height="185" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/News-570x479.jpg/220px-News-570x479.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/News-570x479.jpg/330px-News-570x479.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/News-570x479.jpg/440px-News-570x479.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:News-570x479.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Path to Freedom Tour traveling south on the East Coast Greenway</div></div></div>
<p>Greenway riders in Georgia will use the Coastal Georgia Greenway to travel from South Carolina to Florida. The route travels through <a href="/wiki/Savannah,_Georgia" title="Savannah, Georgia">Savannah</a>, <a href="/wiki/Richmond_Hill,_Georgia" title="Richmond Hill, Georgia">Richmond Hill</a>, <a href="/wiki/Midway,_Georgia" title="Midway, Georgia">Midway</a>, <a href="/wiki/Riceboro,_Georgia" title="Riceboro, Georgia">Riceboro</a>, <a href="/wiki/Darien,_Georgia" title="Darien, Georgia">Darien</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brunswick,_Georgia" title="Brunswick, Georgia">Brunswick</a>, <a href="/wiki/Woodbine,_Georgia" title="Woodbine, Georgia">Woodbine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kingsland,_Georgia" title="Kingsland, Georgia">Kingsland</a>, and <a href="/wiki/St._Marys,_Georgia" title="St. Marys, Georgia">St. Marys</a>. The 160-mile (260 km) route is only 6% off-road but has another 14% in development. There are 41 miles (66 km) of gaps, but efforts are being made to connect the route.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li>Belles Ferry – <a href="/wiki/Savannah,_Georgia" title="Savannah, Georgia">Savannah</a></li>
<li>Triplett Park Trail – Savannah</li>
<li>Chief O.F. Love Trail – <a href="/wiki/Chatham_County,_Georgia" title="Chatham County, Georgia">Chatham County</a></li>
<li>Canebrake Rd Sidepath – Chatham County</li>
<li>Highlander Trail – <a href="/wiki/Darien,_Georgia" title="Darien, Georgia">Darien</a></li>
<li>Marshes of Glynn Trail – <a href="/wiki/Brunswick,_Georgia" title="Brunswick, Georgia">Brunswick</a></li>
<li>White Oak Trail – <a href="/wiki/White_Oak,_Georgia" title="White Oak, Georgia">White Oak</a></li>
<li>Woobine Riverwalk – <a href="/wiki/Woodbine,_Georgia" title="Woodbine, Georgia">Woodbine</a></li>
<li>St. Marys Downtown Trail – <a href="/wiki/St._Marys,_Georgia" title="St. Marys, Georgia">St. Marys</a></li></ul>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:361px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:MetroPath_rail_trail_junction.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3264" data-file-width="4928" height="238" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/MetroPath_rail_trail_junction.JPG/359px-MetroPath_rail_trail_junction.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/MetroPath_rail_trail_junction.JPG/539px-MetroPath_rail_trail_junction.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/MetroPath_rail_trail_junction.JPG/718px-MetroPath_rail_trail_junction.JPG 2x" width="359"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:MetroPath_rail_trail_junction.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Junction of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/MetroPath" title="MetroPath">MetroPath</a> with <a href="/wiki/South_Dade_Rail_Trail" title="South Dade Rail Trail">South Dade Rail Trail</a> in <a href="/wiki/Miami" title="Miami">Miami</a>, <a href="/wiki/Florida" title="Florida">Florida</a></div></div></div><div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:551px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Way_2015-570x205.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="205" data-file-width="570" height="197" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Way_2015-570x205.jpg/549px-Way_2015-570x205.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/e/ee/Way_2015-570x205.jpg 1.5x" width="549"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Way_2015-570x205.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Riders from the 2015 Week a Year Tour</div></div></div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Florida">Florida</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=East_Coast_Greenway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Florida">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The Florida section of the ECG starts in <a href="/wiki/Fernandina_Beach,_Florida" title="Fernandina Beach, Florida">Fernandina Beach</a> and travels south along the coast through small beach towns and major cities, such as <a href="/wiki/Jacksonville,_Florida" title="Jacksonville, Florida">Jacksonville</a> and <a href="/wiki/Miami" title="Miami">Miami</a>. The route continues down through islands and bridges to the southernmost point of the continental United States, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Key_West,_Florida" title="Key West, Florida">Key West</a>. This segment of greenway is 600 miles (970 km) long, the longest of the ECG, and is 31% off-road. There is another 13% in development and another 38% in public control and is to be developed. There are some gaps.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Amelia_Island" title="Amelia Island">Amelia Island</a> Trail – <a href="/wiki/Nassau_County,_Florida" title="Nassau County, Florida">Nassau County</a></li>
<li>River to Sea Trail – <a href="/wiki/Flagler_County,_Florida" title="Flagler County, Florida">Flagler County</a></li>
<li>Jacksonville North Bank Riverwalk – <a href="/wiki/Jacksonville,_Florida" title="Jacksonville, Florida">Jacksonville</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Mayport_Ferry" title="Mayport Ferry">St. Johns River Ferry</a> – <a href="/wiki/Fort_George_Island_Cultural_State_Park" title="Fort George Island Cultural State Park">Ft. George</a> to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mayport,_Florida" title="Mayport, Florida">Mayport</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Timucua" title="Timucua">Timucuan</a> Trail – Jacksonville</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Palatka,_Florida" title="Palatka, Florida">Palatka</a>–<a href="/wiki/St._Augustine,_Florida" title="St. Augustine, Florida">St. Augustine</a> State Trail – <a href="/wiki/St._Johns_County,_Florida" title="St. Johns County, Florida">St. Johns County</a></li>
<li>Mickler Trail – <a href="/wiki/St._Augustine_Beach,_Florida" title="St. Augustine Beach, Florida">St. Augustine Beach</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Halifax_River" title="Halifax River">Halifax River</a> Trail – <a href="/wiki/Holly_Hill,_Florida" title="Holly Hill, Florida">Holly Hill</a> to <a href="/wiki/Daytona_Beach,_Florida" title="Daytona Beach, Florida">Daytona Beach</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Spring_to_Spring_Trail" title="Spring to Spring Trail">Spring-to-Spring Trail</a> – <a href="/wiki/Volusia_County,_Florida" title="Volusia County, Florida">Volusia County</a></li>
<li>East Coast Central Regional Rail Trail – Volusia County</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Florida_State_Road_A1A" title="Florida State Road A1A">A1A</a> Sidepath – <a href="/wiki/Brevard_County,_Florida" title="Brevard County, Florida">Brevard County</a></li>
<li>Prima Vista Blvd Sidepath – <a href="/wiki/St._Lucie_County,_Florida" title="St. Lucie County, Florida">St. Lucie County</a></li>
<li>Walton Rd Sidepath – St. Lucie County</li>
<li>Green River Parkway Trail – <a href="/wiki/Martin_County,_Florida" title="Martin County, Florida">Martin County</a> to <a href="/wiki/Port_St._Lucie,_Florida" title="Port St. Lucie, Florida">Port St. Lucie</a></li>
<li>Seabranch Trail – Martin County</li>
<li>Jupiter Riverwalk – <a href="/wiki/Jupiter,_Florida" title="Jupiter, Florida">Jupiter</a></li>
<li>West Palm Beach Trail – <a href="/wiki/West_Palm_Beach,_Florida" title="West Palm Beach, Florida">West Palm Beach</a></li>
<li>A1A Sidepath – <a href="/wiki/Boca_Raton,_Florida" title="Boca Raton, Florida">Boca Raton</a></li>
<li>Hollywood Broadwalk – <a href="/wiki/Hollywood,_Florida" title="Hollywood, Florida">Hollywood</a></li>
<li>Atlantic Greenway – <a href="/wiki/Miami_Beach,_Florida" title="Miami Beach, Florida">Miami Beach</a></li>
<li>M Path Trail – <a href="/wiki/Miami-Dade_County,_Florida" title="Miami-Dade County, Florida">Miami-Dade County</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/South_Dade_Rail_Trail" title="South Dade Rail Trail">South Dade Rail Trail</a> – Miami-Dade County</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Overseas_Heritage_Trail" title="Overseas Heritage Trail">Overseas Heritage Trail</a> – <a href="/wiki/Key_Largo,_Florida" title="Key Largo, Florida">Key Largo</a> to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Key_West,_Florida" title="Key West, Florida">Key West</a></li></ul>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Lincoln_Pk_ECGW_ribbon_cutting_jeh.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2400" data-file-width="2602" height="203" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Lincoln_Pk_ECGW_ribbon_cutting_jeh.jpg/220px-Lincoln_Pk_ECGW_ribbon_cutting_jeh.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Lincoln_Pk_ECGW_ribbon_cutting_jeh.jpg/330px-Lincoln_Pk_ECGW_ribbon_cutting_jeh.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Lincoln_Pk_ECGW_ribbon_cutting_jeh.jpg/440px-Lincoln_Pk_ECGW_ribbon_cutting_jeh.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Lincoln_Pk_ECGW_ribbon_cutting_jeh.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Jerramiah Healy, Mayor of <a href="/wiki/Jersey_City,_New_Jersey" title="Jersey City, New Jersey">Jersey City</a>, cuts ribbon for a bikeway to <a href="/wiki/Newark,_New_Jersey" title="Newark, New Jersey">Newark</a>.</div></div></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="East_Coast_Greenway_Alliance">East Coast Greenway Alliance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=East_Coast_Greenway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: East Coast Greenway Alliance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The East Coast Greenway Alliance (ECGA) is a nonprofit organization that oversees, but does not own, the greenway. The Alliance is based in <a href="/wiki/Durham,_North_Carolina" title="Durham, North Carolina">Durham, North Carolina</a>, next to the <a href="/wiki/American_Tobacco_Trail" title="American Tobacco Trail">American Tobacco Trail</a>. Six Greenway coordinators work remotely in their regions.
</p><p>The Alliance coordinates the Greenway's growth by working with local, state, regional, and national organizations and agencies. The Alliance is in charge of designating new trail segments and finding routes for the greenway, posting signs designating the path, spreading awareness of the project, and providing maps and information about the greenway.
</p><p>ECGA advocates for safe access to bike paths on roadways and bridges, as well as convenient access to public transportation for cyclists. In addition, the Alliance promotes the use of alternate transportation, such as use of greenways.
</p><p>Learn more at greenway.org.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Events">Events</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=East_Coast_Greenway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Events">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Upcoming events held on or concerning the Greenway include:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li><b>East Coast River Relay</b>, Aug. 24-Oct. 30, 2017. Two months and 3,000 miles of public events in the fall of 2017 to celebrate 25 years, 50 rivers, 1 Greenway.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup></li>
<li><b>Week a Year Bike Tour</b>: October 2017. Participants will travel 300 to 350 miles (480 to 560 km) of Greenway with ECGA staff and other cycling professional services.</li>
<li><b>Southeast Greenways &amp; Trails Summit</b>, Durham, NC, Oct. 1–3. A gathering of greenway advocates and partners to share and learn and shine spotlight on Triangle area's network of greenways.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup></li>
<li>New England Bike-Walk Summit. Boston, MA, April 26–27. A gathering of greenway and advocates and partners.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup></li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Awards">Awards</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=East_Coast_Greenway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Awards">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul><li>Named one of the <a href="/wiki/National_Millennium_Trail" title="National Millennium Trail">National Millennium Trails</a> by the <a href="/wiki/White_House" title="White House">White House</a> in 1999<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Kodak" title="Kodak">Kodak</a> American Greenway Award in 1999 by <a href="/wiki/The_Conservation_Fund" title="The Conservation Fund">The Conservation Fund</a> in Washington, DC, by the <a href="/wiki/National_Geographic_Society" title="National Geographic Society">National Geographic Society</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup></li>
<li>GoSmart Golden Modes Community Impact Award in 2015<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup></li>
<li>GSK IMPACT Award in 2015<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup></li>
<li>Bicycle Friendly Business for 2016 – 2020 by the <a href="/wiki/League_of_American_Bicyclists" title="League of American Bicyclists">League of American Bicyclists</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup></li></ul>
